How much longer?!\" It became clear that the fact that this was an electric car was a non-issue. And so I stopped any notions of meticulous logging and just had fun and stayed present. The car handled the steep grades on the path like a champ. In fact the only thing missing was the roar of an engine struggling to make it up the hill. ;-) Per the attached map below, we stopped twice, breaking the trip into thirds. This gave us an opportunity to eat, switch drivers, refresh\u2026 and of course recharge. In a gas-powered car, at least one of these stops would have been \"optional\" for me\u2026 maybe we'd have broken the trip into halves instead of thirds. But we'd have still stopped to eat, and additionally I'd have definitely needed at least one bio-break and stand-and-stretch. So in reality, there was a bit of a compromise. For our second stop, what might have been a 15 minute pit-stop ended up being longer (by about 40 minutes.) We put the time to good use, and it didn't feel burdensome. I heard a couple of NPR Marketplace correspondents last week describe this tradeoff well. The first said (I paraphrase), \"It's not always appropriate to judge a new, disruptive technology against an incumbent across every dimension. For instance, landlines almost never 'drop calls.'
